[{"id":47684,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/utah-jazz-bonding-together-during-10-game-win-streak","date":"2018-02-14","title":"Utah Jazz a changed, closer team during 10-game win streak","content":" There were no underlying issues when the Utah Jazz took a 104-90 loss to the Atlanta Hawks on the road Jan. 22 . The team simply came out flat and, as a result, fell to 19-28 and looked more on their way for the NBA Draft lottery than a push for a playoff run in the Western Conference. Fast-forward to today and the Jazz are the hottest team in the NBA, winners of 10 straight games as tonight\u2019s game against the Phoenix Suns looms ( 9 ET, NBA League Pass ). It is not often that a team boasting a rookie as a leading scorer (Donovan Mitchell) and that has dealt with injury issues makes a sudden playoff charge. But that\u2019s exactly what the Jazz are doing and Eric Woodyard of The Deseret News digs into how they\u2019ve done it. In short, the Jazz have found some toughness, found togetherness and are in a defensive and offensive zone they\u2019ve lacked all season : * * *"},{"id":47227,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/paul-pierce-kevin-garnetts-number-next-be-retired-boston-celtics","date":"2018-02-14","title":"Paul Pierce: Kevin Garnett's number next to be retired by Boston Celtics","content":" With his number having just been retired by the Celtics , Paul Pierce said he anticipates being joined by one of his key teammates on their 2008 championship teams. \u201cWithout a doubt, (Kevin Garnett\u2019s) number will be retired in Boston,\u201d said Pierce, as reported by ESPN . \u201cIt\u2019s going to happen.\u201d Garnett is undoubtedly one of the greatest players to ever suit up in the NBA, a 15-time All-Star and one of 32 MVP award winners . But he also spent only six of his 17 seasons in Boston, leaving some to question whether he should be honored alongside the likes of Pierce, Bill Russell and Larry Bird. According to Celtics president Danny Ainge, those six seasons were so good \u2014 Garnett made the All-Star team in five of them, with six playoff appearances and the team\u2019s first title in more than 20 years \u2014 that the team has already held informal discussions. Ultimately, Ainge said, the decision to hang Garnett\u2019s No. 5 in the rafters at TD Garden will be made by ownership. \u201cIt was six years of potential championship-caliber teams and All-Star play from KG,\u201d said Ainge. \u201cI think that it was a pretty significant impact he had in those six years.\u201d * * *"},{"id":47592,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/lawrence-frank-jerry-west-tasked-giving-los-angeles-clippers-new-identity-and","date":"2018-02-14","title":"Lawrence Frank, Jerry West tasked with carving out long-lasting identity for Los Angeles Clippers","content":" LOS ANGELES \u2014  For a fortunate few, the love of the game develops very innocently before mushrooming into something bolder and better and suddenly, a basketball career is born. For example, take the Clippers: A teenaged DeAndre Jordan grew too tall for football pads in Texas. Austin Rivers watched his father Doc, the Clippers coach and former NBA player, on TV and took notes. Then there\u2019s the person in charge of running this team. He put funky uniforms in the laundry bin, collected damp socks, made sure the towels were fresh and kept the locker room nice and tidy. \u201cWell, that\u2019s how you start out on the job,\u201d said Lawrence Frank, explaining his to-do list as student manager of his college team at Indiana. \u201cBy the time you\u2019re a senior, you\u2019re assisting the coaches with scouting reports.\u201d The story of Frank\u2019s basketball life, therefore, is how he kept graduating to something more satisfying and challenging as the journey continued. After Indiana he was an assistant coach in college, then in the NBA, then an NBA head coach, and last summer was handed the basketball operations job with the Clippers after a significant restructuring and shakeup at the top of the organization. Beneath the executive two-piece suit, however, lies a basketball dreamer who\u2019s eager to do the grunt work, someone who did so while dealing with the unpredictable whims of the mercurial Bob Knight, and that base will never leave him, Frank says. (Oh, and about Knight: Frank was hired on the spot, sight unseen \u2014 no interview, no nothing \u2014 for his first few coaching jobs out of college because Knight simply placed a call.) \u201cThat was an unbelievable foundation for me, for every step of my career,\u201d he said. \u201cYou appreciate being on the ground floor and it taught me about the chain of command and about respect for others and if you want to be good, it\u2019s about the work you must put into it. You learn the value of teammates, humility, all the things we preach to our kids and teams. Any job isn\u2019t too small.\u201d * More L.A. Week Well, this job Frank has now is fairly ambitious, even more when you consider the hilarious history of the franchise and also the recently unfulfilled era with the dearly departed Chris Paul and Blake Griffin, who left the Clippers with \u2026 what, exactly? That\u2019s the slippery state of the Clippers right now; they can slide in either direction and catch almost nobody by surprise. They do have Jordan, a voracious rebounder and paint enforcer; Lou Williams, an unapologetic gunner and late bloomer; and Tobias Harris, a young scorer who previously played on teams that nobody bothered to watch. And they also have a hazy picture at point guard, upcoming free agency issues with Jordan, and miles between them and those who rule the West. Also, and this must be stressed because after all they are The Clippers , there\u2019s a stigma to deal with. About that reputation: Maybe it\u2019s dead. Maybe it vaporized when former owner Donald Sterling was yanked from power and took with him a legacy of crummy drafts, lousy luck, lost decades and a general sense of ridicule within the NBA. This was the spring of 2014 when Sterling was caught on audio making, to put it mildly, insensitive comments about people who share the same skin color as most of his players. In a warped way, this was a game-changer for a team that has never advanced beyond the second round of the playoffs, if only because it meant the end of Sterling , who made everything he touched turn to aluminum foil. The franchise came to L.A. uninvited from Buffalo by way of San Diego and never really caught L.A.\u2019s passion even after 33 years. Mainly because of Sterling\u2019s reign of error, they\u2019re Cain to the Lakers\u2019 Abel, a team smack in the entertainment capital lacking the sizzle, celebrity following, national branding or championship chops of their more beloved basketball brother. Ron Harper, whose promising career took a wicked turn when he suffered a knee injury less than two months as a Clipper, would respond \u201cLos Angeles\u201d when asked what team he played for. In a sense, much like a young Lawrence Frank, the Clippers have spent most of their NBA existence as the student manager of the league. They\u2019ve clearly taken a few steps backward after being forced to trade Paul last summer to the Rockets and, in a shocking shift of allegiance, sending Griffin to the Pistons a few weeks ago. That doesn\u2019t mean the Clippers aren\u2019t better off in the long run, though. It depends on how much room they create under the salary cap to gain flexibility and the free agents they chase and trades they make. Frank has the advantage of a thick wallet belonging to billionaire owner Steve Ballmer and the ear of the great Jerry West, the team consultant and sounding board. That\u2019s a start. What Frank and the Clippers lack right now is traction. And once again, an identity. \u201cWe know we have something to prove,\u201d said Jordan. The Golden Age of the franchise was from 2013-17 when the Clippers had Griffin, Jordan and Paul; all three were top-five, arguably, at their position over that time. Plus there was JJ Redick and Jamal Crawford, a pair of respected veteran shooters. And also Rivers, regarded as one of the top coaches in the NBA with a championship from Boston. That was, under almost any definition, a championship contender. They had five straight 50-win seasons, the third-best record in the NBA over that stretch \u2026 and went no deeper than the second round of the playoffs. This was their scarlet letter in that \u201cLob City\u201d era, although it must be explained how injuries once again finger-nailed the Clippers\u2019 blackboard, and at all the wrong moments. Of course, there will always be the 2015 second round when their injuries came from squeezing their own throats. That\u2019s when they crumbled to Houston after a 3-1 series lead. Most embarrassing was being up 19 at home in Game 6 and losing to Corey Brewer and Josh Smith with James Harden on the bench. Otherwise, their playoff path was a series of players reaching for body parts and wincing. Paul missed the first two games of that \u201915 series with the Rockets with a bad hamstring suffered in the first round against the Spurs and was never 100 percent vs. Houston. Griffin and Paul missed the 2016 playoffs with a broken finger and a sore quad. Griffin came up lame last spring against the Jazz in the first round and the Clippers were finished. Rivers sighs and says: \u201cThere\u2019s nothing you can do about it, really. The year Chris gets the hamstring injury in the San Antonio series, that\u2019s the only one I think most about, what if he had been healthy for us in the Houston series which came next. \u201cIt\u2019s all health related, this business. The teams that win owe it to good health. When you\u2019re winning titles, you\u2019re healthy, you don\u2019t have guys sitting out.\u201d The Clippers were the last team in the West to beat the Warriors in the playoffs and that was the high-water point of Lob City. Otherwise, beyond the highlight reels and individual honors, significant as they were, there wasn\u2019t much to crow about. Even this year, injuries paid another uninvited visit. In fact, those injuries spooked the club and conspired to make the Clippers re-think their investment in Griffin, whom they gave a five-year, $171 million deal just last summer. They realized they could only grow so much while paying a fortune to a power forward who\u2019s on the wrong side of 30 and a power forward with a significant injury history (most were freakish in nature, but still, they add up). Rivers has done one of his better coaching jobs this season, given the shifting lineups caused by injuries to his son, Danilo Gallinari, Patrick Beverley and others, keeping the Clippers within a few nose hairs of the final playoff spot with a few months to go. \u201cI love this team,\u201d Rivers said. \u201cIt\u2019s a great group to coach. They just play hard. And our ball movement is infectious. They pass so much that everybody wants to join in.\u201d It could be argued that Rivers is more at peace, now that he no longer has the personnel title and the hassles that go with that. He didn\u2019t raise a stink, at least not publicly, when they cut his titles in half (perhaps because they didn\u2019t reduce his pay) and seems content to see what the next chapter brings. It helps that he and Frank have history; Rivers hired Frank as his assistant in Boston and also brought him to the Clippers to serve the same role before the promotion. \u201cDoc and I have such a special relationship because it\u2019s based on honesty,\u201d said Frank. \u201cWe deal with each other openly and honestly. We serve each other. It\u2019s a true partnership. We tell and take the hard truths and we both share the same vision in trying to do what\u2019s in the best interests of the organization. We\u2019re both here to serve each other, the players and the organization. He put me in the front office role. When it was restructured we haven\u2019t skipped a beat. For us, we keep moving forward.\u201d The Clippers padded the front office by adding the expertise of West, who built championship dynasties with the Lakers and Warriors; along with former Oklahoma City Thunder executive Michael Winger and Trent Redden, formerly of the Cavaliers, and the debate amongst them is healthy. \u201cWhen everybody agrees on the same thing, No. 1, it\u2019s an echo chamber and No. 2, someone\u2019s not needed,\u201d said Frank. They did agree two weeks ago that it was time for Griffin to move on, with the biggest nudge coming from West. It wasn\u2019t an easy about-face, of course; Griffin was a five-time All-Star and rescued the franchise from the dumpster when he was drafted in 2011. He sold T-shirts and jerseys, put the club on prime-time TV and, from his jump-over-a-car dunk and catchy commercials, made the Clippers \u2026 cool. But trading Griffin to the star-desperate Pistons was groundbreaking in that it forced the club to try a different approach. The next shakeup could be felt by Jordan, the longest-tenured Clipper who hasn\u2019t been offered a contract extension by the club and isn\u2019t expected to receive one, at least not right away. Jordan has an option next season at $24 million and he\u2019s in a tricky spot. With salary cap money drying up for 2018-19 and most teams suddenly becoming budget conscious, it\u2019s unlikely Jordan will bank that much on the market this summer, even though he\u2019s still a solid rebounder (14 per game over the last five years) and defender and just 29. He can opt-out and get more years, but less annual money, from another team; or he can stay in L.A. and play for the $24 million and then hit the market in 2019. \u201cI\u2019ve been here when it was horrible times, good times and great times,\u201d said Jordan. \u201cBeing here as long as I\u2019ve been here is something I\u2019ve taken pride in.\u201d He paused, then added: \u201cI\u2019ve been loyal,\u201d which is somewhat true; he did try to flee the Clipper ship four years ago when he accepted, then backed out of, a free agent deal with the Mavericks . Surely, Jordan can see the handwriting; with Paul and Griffin gone, what\u2019s stopping the Clippers from washing free of Lob City and starting fresh? All Frank would say is: \u201cWe have a great relationship with DJ and his agent. He\u2019s one of the top players in the league and having another terrific year.\u201d The Clippers\u2019 plan is clear: Get leaner with the cap, and develop younger players while mixing in a few reasonably-priced veterans. That\u2019s why they kept Lou Williams at the trade deadline; when he agreed to a three-year extension at $24 million , it fit the plan. He\u2019s averaging 23 points and five assists this season, by far the most productive of his career, yet he\u2019ll be 32 next season. So the team-friendly money helped the Clippers while the security helped a player who previously bounced around five other teams.  Beyond Jordan, Harris, Williams and Gallinari, the remaining talent is either aging or tapped out or just average. There\u2019s a need for a star, but those type tend to gravitate toward the other team in town. If the Clippers were truly a reflection of ownership during the Donald Sterling years, and if this pattern continues, then the ball belongs to a former software executive who\u2019s balding, wears clothes that scream Jos. A Bank, tends to get goofy after a great play and is worth upwards of $30 billion. We know Steve Ballmer is rightly hailed as a savior in L.A. simply because, if nothing else, he\u2019s clearly not Sterling. But what kind of owner is he, and will he be going forward? There haven\u2019t been any burps since he paid $2 billion for the club four years ago and Ballmer doesn\u2019t appear to be the intrusive type. He also, and rather boldly, stripped Rivers of the personnel duties and brought in West, and you can\u2019t find many in the basketball world who will argue against either of those moves. They indicate that Ballmer is a quick study and is getting the hang of this ownership gig. \u201cWhat Steve has been able to do in a short amount of time has been great,\u201d said Frank. \u201cEveryone sees the passion but don\u2019t get to see the humility, investment and commitment to make this a world class organization. He provides every single resource necessary to all the people who work for the Clippers. We\u2019ve been able to add so many high level people, new resources, technology in a short amount of time. That\u2019s why we\u2019re optimistic about what we are and what we can be.\u201d Frank says Ballmer is a basketball guy beneath the billions, and a boss who holds people accountable, yet is reasonable. \u201cYou see the intelligence but what\u2019s pressing the most is his humility,\u201d Frank said. \u201cPeople\u2019s eyes widen when someone\u2019s worth $30 billion but he\u2019s just a very likable guy. There\u2019s no false pretenses. He\u2019s very direct, honest and connects with people. He wants to do the right things. He loves the game. He\u2019ll watch five games a night, you can pick his brain and bounce ideas and he\u2019ll give you an unfiltered opinion.\u201d Ballmer has retired from the daily role at Microsoft and is living in Los Angeles part-time and tending to all things Clippers. Eventually, though, he must weigh in on the two people still remaining from Lob City: Jordan and Rivers. Both decisions must be run by Ballmer because they involve money and\/or direction. Is a low-post center who can\u2019t create his own shot still worth $20 million-plus in today\u2019s NBA, especially as he drifts toward the other side of 30? Is Rivers the right man for a team that\u2019ll suddenly lean more toward youth and development? Mostly, does Ballmer have all the right people in place under him who\u2019ll steer the club correctly through this transitional stage? \u201cWe want to be very good for a very long time and every decision we make is based on that,\u201d said Frank. \u201cThere\u2019s no one formula to build a team. You must do what\u2019s best to fit your overall vision. If there was one way to build a champion, everybody would be doing it. There\u2019s also timing and an element of luck, some of it circumstantial. You try to plan and make the best informed decision you can.\u201d This isn\u2019t the hapless Clippers you once knew. And it\u2019s not the Clippers of four years ago, either. The goal is to carve out an identity that lasts, not only for decades, but beyond May, for once. Yes, the Clippers are dying to get past the second round of the playoffs. In their present state, however, just reaching the playoffs will be progress. Time has done little to heal those wounds, as Pierce detailed during an appearance with Kevin Garnett, Rajon Rondo, Kendrick Perkins and Glen Davis last year on TNT\u2019s Area 21. \u201cI was initially hurt with the way everything went down,\u201d Pierce said. \u201cI don\u2019t have beef with any of my teammates. While it remains to be seen how Pierce received Allen\u2019s message, that first step has seemingly been taken. His reason why? \u201cI\u2019m saving my right hand for the Lakers.\u201d Bird scored 10 of his 21 field goals against Portland with his left hand, and finished the game with 47 points, 14 rebounds and 11 assists. The Celtics won the game 120-119 in overtime . Two nights later, Bird finished with 22 points, 18 rebounds and seven assists in the Celtics\u2019 105-99 win over the Lakers in L.A. The Celtics went on to win the NBA championship that season , with Bird leading the way for his second NBA Finals MVP award. Wisconsin was No. 1 in the player pool and claimed Jennings, according to Marc Stein of the New York Times . He had been chosen for his first All-Star Game."},{"id":41768,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/new-age-nba-centers-karl-anthony-towns-nikola-jokic-kristaps-porzingis-clint","date":"2018-02-13","title":"Wave of star big men form axis for new age of center play","content":" Maybe it\u2019s time to put \u201cCenter\u201d back on the All-Star ballots. The voting category dedicated to the game\u2019s best big men has been missing since 2013 , removed by the league\u2019s Competition Committee in a nod to a style of play pushing toward the perimeter. There also was an acknowledgement that the very best bigs were roaming the NBA as \u201cpower forwards\u201d and, let\u2019s be honest, a desire to avoid the likes of Jamaal Magloire and Brad Miller as \u201cAll Stars,\u201d mucking up the annual fast-paced, offense-obsessed showcase game. As league exec Stu Jackson said at the time, \u201cIt [the center category] just seemed a little outdated and didn\u2019t represent the way our game has evolved.\u201d As Roy Hibbert, the former Indiana Pacers center who felt his All-Star days were suddenly over (he\u2019d made the 2012 Game): \u201cThat\u2019s bull\u2014-!\u201d Well, get a load of the All-Star rosters now. Joel Embiid, DeMarcus Cousins (injured) and Anthony Davis racked up enough votes to earn starting spots . Al Horford, Karl-Anthony Towns, Draymond Green, Kristaps Porzingis (injured), Kevin Love (injured) and Andre Drummond were chosen reserves or injury replacements. There\u2019s a wide range of sizes, skills and capabilities in that group of nine, but all are, or at various times have been, centers. Just when it looked as if the large fellows were marching dinosaur-style into the NBA\u2019s great tar pit, the league suddenly turned into Jurassic Park. Centers are thriving, with the position hosting a wildly diverse group of players, from traditional, plodding bangers to ball stylists with the shooting and passing skills of wings. \u201cThere\u2019s very talented [big men] now,\u201d former Milwaukee coach Jason Kidd said earlier this season. That night the Bucks were facing Minnesota, and Towns happened to pass by in the hallway where Kidd was talking. \u201cJust talking about Towns as he\u2019s walkin\u2019 by, someone who can play inside, out, put it on the floor,\u201d Kidd said. \u201cCan lead the break. Can pass. Everybody talks about the [3-pointer]. So I think the center position is in a good place. Sometimes we look at the past and how the game has changed, and some of us haven\u2019t changed with the game. But there\u2019s an understanding that everybody can shoot a thiree now. It\u2019s not just about playing inside for twos.\u201d The poster guy for the resurgence at center is the Philadelphia 76ers\u2019 Joel Embiid. At 7-foot and a sturdy 250 pounds, Embiid looks like a throwback big man, with the length and heft to dominate inside. Yet he possesses the ball skills and shooting range of a guard, combined with nimble footwork reminiscent of Houston Rockets legend Hakeem Olajuwon . What\u2019s exciting for the NBA \u2013 and a sign of a style pendulum swinging back \u2013 is the number of promising young big men lining up to challenge both Embiid and any irrational thoughts about a centerless game. Per basketball-reference.com, of the 31 centers and power forwards who were averaging at least 10.0 points and 6.0 rebounds through Monday night (while appearing in at least 30 games), 10 are age 23 or younger . Seven more are 24 or 25. Only six are older than 29. And among the youngest group, only Houston\u2019s Clint Capela and the Portland Trail Blazers\u2019 Jusuf Nurkic are down in the single digits of the 3-point game with traditional big men like the Charlotte Hornets\u2019 Dwight Howard, the LA Clippers\u2019 DeAndre Jordan or the Miami Heat\u2019s Hassan Whiteside. The 10 youngest of those 31 big men have attempted 125.2 shots from the arc this season, compared to 69.6 by the 10 oldest. And that includes Marc Gasol\u2019s 233 and Al Horford\u2019s 175 , which account for 58.6 percent of the older group\u2019s total. Golden State Warriors coach Steve Kerr talked last month about rule changes that made life tougher for traditional post players. \u201cWhen Patrick [Ewing] was playing, you couldn\u2019t double-team the post until the guy got the ball,\u2019\u2019 Kerr said. \u201cYou can do that now \u2014 it\u2019s made posting up much more difficult. \u201cSo rule changes led to an offensive revolution. Led to centers deciding, \u2018I\u2019m going to go shoot threes,\u2019 whether it was Pau Gasol or Mo Speights, Marc Gasol. You see a lot of centers who, three years ago, never took a three and now they\u2019re shooting threes.\u201d Certainly, some old guys have learned new tricks \u2014 Gasol has scored 29.9 percent of his points on 3-pointers since the start of 2016-17, compared to just 0.4 percent through his first eight seasons. But it\u2019s the new guys who are arriving with those tricks as standard equipment. \u201cCertain types of big men [have been legislated out of the game],\u201d Rockets coach Mike D\u2019Antoni said, laughing. \u201cThe ones who aren\u2019t skilled.\u201d D\u2019Antoni doesn\u2019t need his centers to launch 3-pointers when he has shooters like James Harden, Chris Paul, Trevor Ariza and Ryan Anderson. And, the Rockets take more 3-pointers ( 42.6 ) than any team in the league. Yet in Capela, D\u2019Antoni has the perfect complementary big. \u201cIt would be nice if you could post up, but that\u2019s not what we\u2019re looking for,\u201d said the Rockets coach. \u201cTo me, a big man has to be able to guard on the perimeter. If he can\u2019t do that, if he can\u2019t run the pick-and-roll and have good hands and finish above the rim, that makes it tough. \u201cThe players have changed, not the game. The big men aren\u2019t going away, they\u2019re just getting better.\u201d Towns is typical of a generation of big men for whom size, formerly an easy advantage, loomed as a possible liability in today\u2019s NBA if it weren\u2019t bundled with superior basketball skills. \u201cWhen I was younger, I was taught to be as versatile as possible,\u201d Towns said. \u201cIf you\u2019re versatile, there\u2019s no reason a coach can\u2019t have you in the game. That\u2019s what my dad\u2019s philosophy was, so from a young age, he taught me to be a guard first and a big second, though I don\u2019t think he had a crystal ball to be able to see what the NBA would become.\u201d Growing up, Towns admired the games of players such as Dirk Nowitzki, Kevin Garnett and Magic Johnson \u2014 all guys who notably \u201cplayed smaller\u201d than their actual sizes. \u201cI wanted to shoot like Dirk, I wanted to play defense like KG, I wanted to be \u2018Showtime\u2019 like Magic,\u201d Towns said. \u201cAs bigs, we all understand that to be the driving force of bringing back the big men, we have to be doing our jobs and continue to get better every day. It\u2019s up to us. Obviously, we have to adapt with the game. We can\u2019t change it back to the way it was. But we can still implement old-school philosophies into the modern game.\u201d Embiid already has made his reputation, being voted in as a starter for Sunday\u2019s All-Star Game . Here are a handful of other young centers who have made size desirable again in a league that fell in love with small ball: Vitals: 7 feet, 244 pounds Key stat:  NBA-leading 49 double-doubles Towns\u2019 offensive repertoire, at his height, is as strong as Embiid\u2019s. And if you see flashes of other big men in his game, well, that\u2019s very much by design. From Shaquille O\u2019Neal to Sam Perkins to Rik Smits, the Wolves center has tried to learn from the best. \u201cOne of the things that has benefited me in my career is being part of the new age of technology,\u201d Towns said. \u201cThe ability growing up to get on the Internet at friends\u2019 houses and go on YouTube and watch videos of great players. Just watching highlights \u2014 Kevin McHale doing his \u2018slippery eel\u2019 and Tim Duncan with his fundamentals . Just the other day I was looking at Kareem Abdul-Jabbar and his hook shot.\u201d Minnesota coach Tom Thibodeau tries to incorporate Towns\u2019 versatility. Now if only he was as effective defensively. Towns leads the NBA in fouls ( 195 through Monday ) and often isn\u2019t a conscientious and aware defender. When he takes that next step in his game, the Wolves can take a bigger step in the standings. Vitals: 6-foot-11, 243 pounds Key stat : Third in blocks per game (2.1) past two seasons. Turner, the Pacers\u2019 young big, claims to have seen the game transform into \u201cpositionless basketball\u201d just in his three NBA seasons. \u201cI think my rookie year was when we saw a lot of big guys \u2014 Brook Lopez, Marc Gasol \u2014 shooting threes. It has happened fast,\u201d Turner said. \u201cYou see a lot of big men doing a little bit of everything now.\u201d Turner feels he adapted quickly. A 21.4 percent 3-point shooter as a rookie, he\u2019s at 35 percent this season . He considers himself an elite shot blocker and says, \u201cI\u2019m confident in my ability to guard on the perimeter and protect the paint.\u201d Injuries and inconsistency have slowed Turner\u2019s development, and some would like to see him work more on his inside game. He shares some of the Pacers\u2019 big-man duties with Domantas Sabonis, son of Hall of Famer Arvydas Sabonis and another of the current gifted young bigs. Vitals: 6-foot-10, 240 pounds Key stat : Leads NBA in 2FG% (.657) Capela suits the Rockets\u2019 high-octane attack as well as they suit him. He doesn\u2019t dawdle at the 3-point line, instead converting at a high rate on lobs and layups. \u201cI like to run the floor, set pick-and-rolls, and move hard and fast,\u201d said Capela, who spent much of his rookie season with the Rio Grande Valley Vipers in the G League . \u201cAlways quick decisions. That brings my team a pace that helps to get our shooters open, to get wide open threes. It also helps me to get dunks.\u201d Capela\u2019s efficiency is impressive too, given the 27.1 minutes he averages. On Feb. 9 vs. the Nuggets, he became the first player to get at least 20 points and 25 rebounds in 29 minutes or fewer . After a victory over Dallas, Paul raved about Capela\u2019s value to their club. \u201cMe and James probably on him more than anyone else because he\u2019s really the backbone of this team,\u201d Paul recently told NBA TV. \u201cWithout him rolling to the basket, without him defending the paint \u2026 CC is the guy.\u201d Vitals: 6-foot-10, 250 pounds Key stat:  Leads centers in assists (5.6 apg) By the numbers, Jokic\u2019s 2017-18 season isn\u2019t much better than his breakout in 2016-17. But the Nuggets are positioned for a postseason berth and the big man\u2019s work as a \u201cpoint center\u201d is a big reason why. Jokic has averaged 7.8 assists in triggering Denver\u2019s offense and leading it to seven victories in 10 games entering Tuesday. He has contributed 18.0 points and 10.7 rebounds in that stretch, too. The Serbian will turn 23 on Feb. 19 and ranks 14th in the league in total touches . But the key to his deft passing is how swiftly he makes his decisions and moves the ball along. \u201cHe picks teams apart with his passing ability,\u201d Turner said. \u201cYou never know when he\u2019s going to shoot it, when he\u2019s going to pass it. Those kind of big men, who are able to play-make, they\u2019re the toughest to guard.\u201d Vitals: 7-foot-3, 240 pounds Key stat : 2.4 blocks per game (tied 1st in NBA) Prior to blowing out his ACL last week , Porzingis was having a monster season, with career highs in scoring (22.7 ppg), blocks (2.4 bpg) and 3-point shooting (39.5 percent). He made history on Dec. 12 when he became the first player in league history with at least 35 points, 10 rebounds, five blocks and five 3-pointers in a game. \u201cHe shoots it so well, you\u2019ve got to respect his range out there,\u201d Turner said. \u201cBut he can also do it down low, especially when he has smaller guys on him.\u201d Porzingis\u2019 injury forced the Knicks to reassess this season, shifting their emphasis away from playoff thoughts to a deeper dive into rebuilding. His rehab timeline will eat into 2018-19 too, though even another 10 or 12 months on the side shouldn\u2019t prevent \u201cThe Unicorn\u201d from taking his place near the top of the NBA\u2019s young hybrid bigs. \u201cIt seems like [it\u2019s a big hurdle], but in the big scheme of things, the guy\u2019s going to play 15, 18 years in this league,\u201d Knicks coach Jeff Hornacek told reporters Monday. \u201cHe\u2019s 22 years old. It\u2019s a bit of a mountain he has to climb for a year. He\u2019ll look back at this and probably be glad he went through it and got stronger. When you hit adversity and bounce back, it says a lot about your character.\u201d * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Joe Vardon of Cleveland.com has more : * * *"},{"id":41791,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/los-angeles-lakers-revival-magic-johnson-rob-pelinka-lonzo-ball-kyle-kuzma","date":"2018-02-13","title":"Showtime: Magic Johnson on mission to take Los Angeles Lakers back to pinnacle of success","content":" LOS ANGELES \u2014 On a typical night, the most besieged person on the Los Angeles Lakers poses for pictures, signs autographs, is followed around the Staples Center, shakes hands, gives hi-fives and has A-list courtside celebrities asking if their people can call his people. The catch is he hasn\u2019t thrown a no-look pass in 22 years or won a championship in 30. Magic Johnson is now decades removed from \u201cShowtime\u201d \u2014 although you wouldn\u2019t know it by the love he still gets in a town where fame fizzles once careers die. Now in his first season as team president, he remains the everlasting smiling face of the organization, and this is precisely why he rushed back to rescue the Lakers last February . He needs and wants players who can replace him. If that\u2019s possible. And so, Magic is on an ambitious mission to create stars and find them, which is something the Lakers have always done in their rich history. There is perhaps no NBA franchise that reflects the city it represents more than the Lakers do. Flashy and transcendent, magnetic and entertaining, the greats followed in a neat and convenient succession: first Elgin Baylor , then Jerry West , Wilt Chamberlain , Kareem Abdul-Jabbar , Magic Johnson , James Worthy , Kobe Bryant ( in No. 8 ), Shaquille O\u2019Neal and Kobe Bryant ( in No. 24 ). They formed the bedrock upon which the franchise and its 16 championships was built. When those names suddenly became Timofey Mozgov, Luol Deng and another Johnson (not Magic, but Wesley), and the Lakers couldn\u2019t even make the playoffs anymore. The aura vaporized and the pain felt by those with a connection to the franchise was eye-gouging. * More L.A. Week Nobody was irritated more than Johnson, by then a wildly successful businessman, TV personality and partial owner of the Los Angeles Dodgers . Whoa, baseball? Seriously, that\u2019s where Magic was spending his time until he heard his true calling, a desperate Jeanie Buss on Line One. \u201cIt was hard for me to sit back and see what was going on, the team losing and doing so without a clear vision,\u201d Johnson said recently. When he retired from the Lakers, he never really left them; they remained in his thoughts, his heart and his financial portfolio (Magic had a small slice of the team until he sold it in 2010 to eventually to buy into the Dodgers). When the team began to tailspin five seasons ago and won just 27, 21 and 17 games (in 2013-14, \u201914-15 and \u201915-16, resepectively), with a roster and a salary cap in flames, one of the Lakers\u2019 biggest critics was \u2026 Magic. Tough love was expressed through social media, where Magic was almost Donald Trump-like on Twitter, taking shots at players, coaches and especially The Brother of Jeanie, who was responsible for the fall. Jim Buss was low-hanging fruit; the more hapless the Lakers looked on his watch, the more that baseball cap slid down over his eyes. A non-bloody coup ensued within the Buss family , with Jeanie flexing her right to swipe control of the Lakers , akin to a sibling wrestling the remote control during TV time, and her first order of business was to ask for, and get, an assist from someone who made that an art form. So this is where we are: Jeanie, Magic, general manager and former Bryant agent Rob Pelinka, Kyle Kuzma, Lonzo Ball, Brandon Ingram, Paul George rumors, LeBron James dreams and uninvited guest LaVar Ball, all conspiring to revive the one franchise that the NBA needs on the floor in May and June if possible. \u201cThe Lakers have the No. 1 fan base in the NBA so it\u2019s good for the league when the Lakers are in contention,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cThat\u2019s what we\u2019re building towards. And we\u2019ll get there.\u201d Perhaps. But the how and the when are what will make this push to prominence a fascinating one. The shot-callers on the Lakers all have a working history with each other. That, on the surface, seems an advantage. There are no introductions needed between Magic, Jeanie Buss and Pelinka. Johnson and Buss met as teenagers. The bond between them was the late Lakers owner Jerry Buss , who mentored both. Johnson and Jeanie have adopted Buss\u2019 philosophies about money and business and running the Lakers. Jeanie Buss oversaw the completion last spring of a new state-of-the-art training center with all the sweet touches (including a barbershop!), proof of the family\u2019s financial commitment to ensure the Lakers have the best of everything. She told Magic and Pelinka to fix the product on the floor and everything else will be provided. \u201cJeanie Buss has done a tremendous job keeping the vision of her father and the hope alive with the Lakers,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cShe\u2019s all about titles. We\u2019ve got everything in place. And people can see that. Who else can say they\u2019ve been losing for four years and still have sellout crowds?\u201d Because he can run the Lakers without restrictions or push-back from above, Magic was only too thrilled to take the wheel. Put aside, for a moment, baseball and gourmet coffee and movie theaters (his other business ventures); Magic was trained for basketball. Of course, just because you\u2019ve won six championships (including his NCAA title), an Olympic gold medal and put lumps in people\u2019s throats, that doesn\u2019t automatically translate into front-office brilliance. West aside, the championship track record for Hall of Fame players-turned-executives isn\u2019t very encouraging. Magic\u2019s eternal basketball twin brother, Larry Bird, finally surrendered last year after an executive run with the hometown Pacers. He had his moments there (three conference finals, an Executive of the Year award in 2011-12), but couldn\u2019t match what he did as a player and didn\u2019t produce a ring. Isiah Thomas, whose friendship with Magic was freshly rekindled recently , had a forgotten run as president of the New York Knicks. While Thomas wasn\u2019t the sole reason the Knicks couldn\u2019t produce a winner, he became a symbol of a lost era, fair or not, among New Yorkers. Then there\u2019s Michael Jordan, still trying to gain traction as owner of the Charlotte Hornets, who seem no closer to sipping champagne now than when he first took ownership of the team in 2010 . Again, the similarities are stark: All-time great player, massively successful businessman (Jordan Brand, commercials) and, so far anyway, unsatisfied basketball bossman. Is this a curse from the Basketball Gods or merely a coincidence? What does Magic know about running a team that the other Hall of Famers didn\u2019t, or don\u2019t? That\u2019s fair to ask. Pelinka can\u2019t speak for them, but he can for Magic. \u201cMagic is relentless in his pursuit of excellence,\u201d Pelinka said. \u201cMagic is the most positive and enthusiastic person I\u2019ve ever come across. Every day he gets up at 4 and works out and then he starts calling me at 6 with ideas and vision. He\u2019s a \u2018vision-caster extraordinaire.\u2019 I like to do the ground work to make sure his vision comes to life.\u201d Pelinka is making the ambitious leap from A-list player agent to general manager, a transition that appears seamless. He crunched numbers with Buss about contracts for Bryant. He brings the nuts and bolts knowledge about the agent culture, negotiating and the salary cap, which frees up Magic to spend more time studying talent. \u201cAfter so many years representing players who\u2019ve been through here I had a natural working relationship with Jeanie,\u201d Pelinka said. \u201cIt seemed a natural progression with her and then to have known Magic so well from being in LA, I have lots of touch points with him. There was just a real common DNA and common vision. The three of us believe in collaboration and round-tabling ideas. We\u2019ve tried to create a structure that\u2019s not bureaucratic. It\u2019s the wheel philosophy. We\u2019re all spokes on the wheel and when the spokes stay strong the wheel stays strong.\u201d Pelinka has other claims to fame. He was a reserve player on the Fab Five team at Michigan, which first exposed him to stars. And he\u2019s a dead ringer for heart-throb actor Rob Lowe; no doubt Pelinka has stories about being approached in LA by strange women biting their pearls. But maybe the best gift that prepared him for the road ahead came when his wife handed him a song by gospel singer Amy Grant, conveniently titled \u201cTakes A Little Time\u201d which includes these lyrics: To get your feet back on the ground, it takes a little time sometimes, It takes a little time sometimes to get the Titanic turned back around. Buss, Magic and Pelinka put their faith in Luke Walton, a first-time coach (not counting his half-season stand-in for Steve Kerr with the Warriors in 2015-16) who can grow into the role. Nobody panicked last month when the Lakers endured a nine-game losing streak, the defense turned sour and Walton\u2019s job security became an issue outside of the organization, not within it. They haven\u2019t forgotten the respect Walton received from Klay Thompson, Stephen Curry and Draymond Green with the Warriors. Also, Walton got good reviews from O\u2019Neal and Bryant on those Lakers championship teams of 2008 and \u201809. If he can work well with superstars, the feeling is, he can work with anyone. \u201cI believe in this group and believe in the fact that when you have repetition and hard work and unselfish players, good things will happen,\u201d Walton said. \u201cIt takes patience and commitment and I think we have all those things in the organization.\u201d They have a Hall of Fame guy, a former ace agent, a basketball lifer as coach and a Buss, all on the top floor of the basketball office. That, they believe, is a winning combo. \u201cThe Lakers have had extreme glory,\u201d Pelinka said. \u201cThe last 2-3 years have been rough and it\u2019s going to take a little time to turn that around. The beauty is we really worked hard to get a great draft class and worked hard with this young core of guys that bring the promise and hope that people see. We have a strong confidence that we\u2019re going to get this done.\u201d Kuzma can\u2019t explain how he felt when Magic dropped that \u201cjunior, junior\u201d sky hook against the Celtics in Game 4 of the 1987 Finals because you cannot describe what you never saw. Kuzma wasn\u2019t born until three years after Magic retired, typical of the team\u2019s \u201cCrib Core\u201d that only knows Magic from what their parents told them. \u201cKobe,\u201d answers Kuzma, when asked what Laker left the best impression on him. \u201cAnd I only remember Jordan with the Wizards.\u201d That\u2019s what the Lakers are dealing with in their locker room, and it\u2019s all positive. Because if Kuzma, Ball and Ingram are indeed keepers, then the Lakers\u2019 work is already halfway done. Given their ages \u2014 all 22 and under \u2014 and small sample-sized looks at their talent, these three can grow organically and develop the same bond as others did before them. Johnson and Pelinka seemingly had a robust Draft debut last summer , getting Ball, swinging a deal that brought Kuzma while also adding Josh Hart . Some luck was involved, of course, as the lottery fell in the Lakers\u2019 favor and they kept a first-round pick that would\u2019ve gone to the Philadelphia 76ers. Ball, Hart and Kuzma are relatively productive and on rookie deals, allowing the Lakers to spend on free agents or absorb heavier contracts via trades. Kuzma, the Lakers\u2019 second-leading scorer ( 15.7 points per game ), is supremely athletic and confident. He can score in a variety of way and is a worker bee defensively. Among this rookie trio, he has the most star sparkle, which others have noticed. Perhaps the biggest compliment Kuzma received was getting an approving postgame hug and head tap from the likes of Kevin Durant. \u201cEvery other game it\u2019s somebody else,\u201d Kuzma said with a grin. \u201cKD had some good things to say. I just try to go out there and play as hard as possible. Being a Laker and getting this much playing time is something I don\u2019t take for granted. A lot of rookies don\u2019t get the chance to play right away. It means a lot that the coaching staff and organization has a lot of faith in me.\u201d If you heard Ingram\u2019s name mentioned in any trades, it didn\u2019t come from the organization. He\u2019s stretchy and bouncy, and his improving  mid-range shot and growing confidence can cause matchup issues with small forwards. Whether he\u2019ll ever add biceps and a beast mentality to see minutes at power forward is questionable and Ingram is lacking as a rebounder ( 5.3 rpg this season in 33.9 mpg ) and rim protector ( 36 blocks in 40 games ). Ball is the Lakers\u2019 highest-drafted point guard since Russell ( No. 2 in 2015 Draft ), but both were the highest drafted Lakers point guard since Johnson in 1979 ( No. 1 overall ). But that\u2019s the least of the burdens Ball carries. Johnson had good intentions when he predicted Ball\u2019s jersey would hang from the rafters one day . But it only intensified the premature public expectations when Ball\u2019s shooting mechanics and accuracy became serious issues to start 2017-18. The basketball world was quick to proclaim Ball as the second-best Lakers rookie after Kuzma, which rings true \u2026 in the short-term anyway. And then LaVar Ball, thirsty for fame, took shots at his son\u2019s teammates and coach . If anything, the Lakers are comforted by seeing how the kid deals with the madness. He\u2019s amazingly level-headed, and this will serve him well when and if the Lakers start to win big on his watch. His floor vision and passing instincts are constantly applauded by opponents. (He\u2019s already got two triple-doubles this season .) And remember, he just turned 20. Most important, he\u2019s well-liked in the locker room and his teammates are giving him room to grow into a leadership role. \u201cThey tell me stay positive when things aren\u2019t going right, to speak up when I need to and encourage me,\u201d Ball said. \u201cIt makes it easy for me.\u201d Ball, Kuzma and Ingram must also cope with the losing that comes with a developing team \u2014 and they\u2019ve put that in perspective. \u201cI think when you win so much in high school and college it\u2019s disappointing to go through, but it\u2019s going to make us stronger as we go through this journey, stronger and tougher,\u201d Ingram said. \u201cI\u2019m comforted by what we do in practice every day. Eventually it\u2019ll come over to the games. Eventually you get tired of losing.\u201d Kuzma promises: \u201cWe\u2019ll figure it out in the next two years. Or less.\u201d This is the most important summer in Lakers history since 1996 when they swung a draft-day trade for Bryant and signed O\u2019Neal . It\u2019s all because they have a healthy salary cap situation, thanks to the Magic-Pelinka-led trades with Brooklyn (last summer) and Cleveland (last week). When the Lakers dialed the Nets and unloaded Mozgov\u2019s bloated contract, it earned them Lopez (on an expiring deal) and the chance to draft Kuzma (who is a steal of a player on a rookie contract). It was brilliant, in hindsight. \u201cI wouldn\u2019t have made that move if I didn\u2019t think we could use that money (this summer),\u201d Johnson said. The Lakers then doubled-down when they sent Jordan Clarkson\u2019s big deal and Larry Nance Jr. (on his rookie deal) to the Cavs in return for Isaiah Thomas and Channing Frye , whose contracts expire this summer. They also grabbed Cleveland\u2019s No. 1 pick in the process, which replaces the first-rounder that was sacrificed by the Jim Buss-Lakers. Once again, it was a money-wise move by Magic and Pelinka and heightens their belief that someone worthy is coming their way this summer or next. Johnson stresses that if the Lakers don\u2019t load up this July, they\u2019ll save some cash for the summer of \u201919. That\u2019s when All-Stars like Kawhi Leonard and Klay Thompson hit the market. Projections have the Lakers with roughly $47 million to dangle this summer. That could swell towards $70 million if, as expected, they let Lopez and Kentavious Caldwell-Pope walk and use the stretch provision on Deng\u2019s contract. There\u2019s also the chance they open more money by not re-signing restricted free agent Julius Randle, which is a tougher call. Randle is in the midst of a mini-breakout season and quickly raising his value to the Lakers. They\u2019ll do whatever, if it means adding James and George, the two most logical free agents this summer and also the best by far. Another GM believes the Lakers will chase New Orleans Pelicans star DeMarcus Cousins hard this summer, even though Cousins is mending from Achilles surgery . If anything, the GM said, the injury could make it easier for the Pelicans to back away if the Laker offer is big enough. \u201cWe\u2019ve got some good young players and then you add some veterans,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cYou look at what Jimmy Butler meant to Minnesota and Kyrie Irving to Boston. Look at their record before they got there and now. They needed a star to take them to the next level. That\u2019s all we need here. We get that, and we\u2019re like Minnesota and like Boston and we become one of the teams that can contend. \u201cThose (free agents this summer) can see that. They\u2019re like, `Man, this young talent they have? And I can put myself in that lineup? We can be good together.\u2019 \u201d The last major upgrade the Lakers tried \u2014 back in 2012 \u2014 went bust. Trading for Dwight Howard and Steve Nash proved both were too hurt and beyond their prime and, as a result, Kobe\u2019s final years weren\u2019t maximized. Johnson says it\u2019s different now, with a new regime in place. \u201cFree agents and their agents know we\u2019re serious about winning,\u201d he said. \u201cThere\u2019s a guy in place that knows how to win and will take care of their guys.\u201d It\u2019s one thing to have young talent and cap space; quite another if you have those assets and someone who knows what to do with it. The Warriors\u2019 worst nightmare is if Johnson knows what to do with this. The man who wants to win also wants to take his time, which sounds like a contradiction until he explains: \u201cYou can\u2019t get it all at one time,\u201d he said. \u201cYou have to build, and so we don\u2019t want to do some stupid trade that could make us good right now but can\u2019t build toward contention for championships. So I\u2019m going to a build it the right way.\u201d What Magic Johnson really wants is to walk into the Stapes Center and get trampled by fans chasing one of his players for selfies. That would be bad for the ego, great for the Lakers. * * * Veteran NBA writer Shaun Powell has worked for newspapers and other publications for more than 25 years. In a pretty stunning series of trades, the Cavs sent out six players and brought in four, getting younger and, more importantly, bigger. Time will tell if Thursday\u2019s moves help keep LeBron James in Cleveland beyond this season, and until Kevin Love gets back, we won\u2019t know what this roster can really do. But improvement, especially on the defensive end of the floor, needs to start now. The East remains wide open, not only because the Cavs have been so bad, but because the Boston Celtics and Toronto Raptors are both better than they were last season. The Celtics have the league\u2019s best defense and Kyrie Irving late in games. The Raptors remain the only team that ranks in the top five in both offensive and defensive efficiency, have the league\u2019s best bench , and now hold the No. 1 spot in the standings . If you have an issue with the rankings, or have a question or comment for John Schuhmann, send him an e-mail or contact him via Twitter . * * *"},{"id":47865,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/morning-tip-assessing-2018-trade-deadline-cleveland-cavaliers-houston-rockets-la","date":"2018-02-12","title":"Twenty takeaways from an NBA trade deadline that (mostly) did not disappoint","content":" Pretty decent NBA trade deadline, amirite? Considering so many teams were determined to hold onto their first-round picks at all costs \u2014 costs being a big deal in the $200 million-plus max deals world of today\u2019s NBA \u2014 any trades at all would have made for a good, exciting day. And then Cavaliers GM Koby Altman went all Al Capone with the bat on fools. Cleveland\u2019s implosion merited taking a blowtorch to the roster, and Altman did that, in a day that centered on the Cavs\u2019 remaking of the roster, but was fascinating by not only what happened, but what didn\u2019t. With so many teams bunched up in both conferences in the playoff race, every one of them would have been justified making a deal. But the days of renting a player for a couple of months for the stretch drive are over. Almost every team has a superstar, or is at least paying their best player like one. And the 2016 spending orgy continues to have ramifications. The outlay from that summer, in large part, has put two-thirds of the league well over the salary cap, with a number of those 20 teams either hard-capped or perilously close to being so. It made maneuvering this year difficult, if not impossible. No role player was worth a team going over the tax apron, or over the tax threshold \u2014 especially if a team would become a repeater tax paying team by doing so. And yet, teams made moves, and not insignifcant ones. (The Blake Griffin trade to the Detroit Pistons , even though it technically was made the week before the deadline, was close enough to it here to be considered a deadline deal.) Because, as ever, it\u2019s ridiculous to assign \u2019\u2019winners\u201d and \u2019\u2019losers\u201d a minute after a trade was made, it\u2019s more accurate to simply observe that some people benefitted from the trades that were made, on and off the court, while others did not, at least immediately. To paraphrase Al Pacino in the Michael Mann film about whistle blower\/hero Jeffrey Wiegand, \u201cThe Insider\u201d \u2026 1. Altman, reconsidered: Cleveland\u2019s rookie GM had so many things to prove in what was a seemingly impossible spot in his first NBA go-round as the Cavs\u2019 boss. In fact, he was derided as not even being the boss, the notion being that Dan Gilbert was getting his inner Jerry Jones on and making personnel decisions as well as owning the team. Altman got heat nationally for holding out for more from Boston before pulling the trigger on the Kyrie Irving trade, then was pilloried for what he got in the deal, then was pilloried for not trading the most important piece of the deal \u2014 the unprotected 2018 first-round pick from Brooklyn that the Celtics had held onto for years before including it to get Irving \u2014 for a short-term fix. And as the Cavs continued to struggle and look less and less like a contender in January, Altman was dismissed altogether as a coatholder for Cavs owner Dan Gilbert, who was thought to be the \u2019real\u2019 GM in Cleveland. But Altman had his say when it mattered last Thursday , as he pulled the trigger on simultaneous deals that took a blowtorch to the old roster, made the team younger and longer and gave it a foundation for the future regardless of what LeBron decides to do this summer \u2014 while not sacrificing the Brooklyn pick. (And, it must be said, all this happened because Gilbert agreed to take on still more luxury tax payments \u2014 another $7 million \u2014 for this year.) Out went Isaiah Thomas and Channning Frye , Jae Crowder and Iman Shumpert , Derrick Rose and Dwyane Wade (the last a sop to Wade that allows him to finish his career in Miami, where everyone wanted\/hoped he would). In came Jordan Clarkson and Larry Nance, Jr., Rodney Hood and George Hill, Hill being the only one over 30. Hood will be a restricted free agent at season\u2019s end but the Cavs are almost certain to keep him and\/or match any offer for him. That would leave Cleveland with Hill, Hood, Clarkson, Kevin Love, Tristan Thompson, Nance, J.R. Smith, Kyle Korver and rookie Cedi Osman all signed for 2018-19, along with whomever Cleveland takes with Brooklyn\u2019s pick, regardless of whether James is there or not. That may not be a championship contending core, but it\u2019s not nothing, either. And, yes, Altman opened the door to the Lakers being able to make a compelling pitch to James to leave Cleveland. But that\u2019s life in the big city. You can\u2019t make a deal because of what it might do to you down the road; you have to improve the team you have. And, Altman did. If James walks, the Cavs now have a post-LeBron future that would be vastly different from the one they had after he left the first time 2010 . 2. LeBron James, revitalized: It was obvious to anyone paying attention that James\u2019 spirit was sapped in the last couple of weeks. His defense bordered on nonexistent; his offensive output collapsed, as he made just 13 3-pointers in 14 games and shot a horrific 22 percent from 3-point range in January. His plus-minus in January, per basketball-reference.com, was -8.3, the worst of his career in a full month\u2019s slate of games. He didn\u2019t believe in the team that Altman had put around him. We will find out what he thinks of his new, younger brethren in due time, but make no mistake \u2014 he\u2019s once again engaged, as his 65th career triple-double Friday in Atlanta showed. And an engaged LeBron can take any group to The Finals. 3. Unnamed ESPN Executive, again hopeful: See No. 2. Whoever ultimately replaces John Skipper, the Four-Letter\u2019s longtime president who suddenly resigned last December , will cry Kevin Hart-sized tears of joy if the Cavs re-ignite and find themselves in a fourth straight Finals against the Golden State Warriors, or face \u201dThe Beard\u201d and \u201dCP3\u201d, in June. Nothing against the Boston Celtics or Toronto Raptors, but LeBron is gold-plated ratings magma, which ABC\/ESPN have ridden to wildly successful numbers the last three years in June, among the best for Finals games since Michael Jordan\u2019s days in Chicago. 4. Daryl Morey, sitting pretty: The Warriors didn\u2019t make a move at the trade deadline to bolster what has been a shaky bench, leaving Morey\u2019s Houston Rockets right where they were before the deadline: right on Golden State\u2019s heels. Getting a post-buyout commit from Joe Johnson also keeps him from going to the Warriors, who coveted his low-post abilities as a small-ball four just as the Rockets did. Morey has methodically built his team to this point since getting Harden: Houston, right now, is a real and credible threat to topple Golden State in the Western Conference. 5. Derrick Favors, queued up: The 26-year-old power forward didn\u2019t get traded, as many around the league figured he would once Utah didn\u2019t give an extension last fall. But with Gordon Hayward and Hill already gone from last year\u2019s roster, and with Hood getting dealt to Cleveland, there aren\u2019t many parts of the existing Jazz nucleus left that Utah has to pay signficant dollars. They already have Rudy Gobert, Joe Ingles and Ricky Rubio inked for 2018-19 at a total outlay of around $51 million, with another $11 million due Alec Burks if Utah keeps him. It then stands to reason that Favors, with full Bird rights in Utah, could be in line for some of that money in July that the Jazz offered Hayward last year. Favors has played extremely well next to Gobert when both have been healthy, and he\u2019s been outstanding during Utah\u2019s nine-game win streak . If he doesn\u2019t stay in Salt Lake City, he\u2019ll be among the top free-agent big men available this summer.  6. Jeanie Buss, Tinseltown Boss: Cleveland took on Clarkson\u2019s $12.5 million for 2018-19 in the Thomas deal. Doing so puts the Lakers back in business this summer, giving them the option to make max offers to two free agents at the same time. So, after the Lakers\u2019 president fired her brother, Jim, and former GM Mitch Kupchak last year , and installing Magic Johnson and Rob Pelinka in their place , Jeanie Buss has her hand-picked management team in place, plenty of cap room and some promising young guys around which to build. The Lakers have a story to tell that should be compelling. They\u2019ve struck out on free agent after free agent for the last several years, sounding out of touch and tone deaf to elite players and their representatives. It\u2019s Showtime. 7. James Ennis, unearthed: The fourth-year forward was having a solid though relatively anonymous season in Memphis, averaging almost seven points off the bench in 23 minutes a game. A lot of teams were trying to get him at the deadline. The Pistons did , to finish a solid fortnight of trades that revamped their roster and injected life into the franchise as they were sinking in the Eastern Conference. Ennis doesn\u2019t have the start power of Griffin and he\u2019s not as familiar with coach Stan Van Gundy as Jameer Nelson is. But the 27-year-old is going to help the Pistons in the last months of the regular season, as they fight for a playoff spot. 8. Mike Malone, keeping the band together: Denver was much less active at the deadline than many thought the Nuggets would be. In the end, they only moved guard Emmanuel Mudiay , who had fallen out of favor and the rotatiion anyway with Jamal Murray assuming the point. The Nuggets didn\u2019t move Will Barton, Wilson Chandler or Kenneth Faried, all of whom had suitors, and they\u2019re expecting Paul Millsap back no later than early March. So Malone, the Nuggets\u2019 coach, has his team essentially in place for the stretch run, which should result in a playoff berth if Denver can stay healthy and Millsap doesn\u2019t have any relapses. And no one at the top of the West wants to see Murray, Gary Harris, Nikola Jokic and company in the first round.  9. Hornets fans, not abandoned: Some around the Association figured that Charlotte, once it let it be known it would listen to offers for Kemba Walker , would have to move him before the deadline. After all, the Hornets don\u2019t have much of a chance at the playoffs this year, and Walker is rapidly approaching free agency in 2019. The idea was, make a good deal for him now (maybe to his native New York) and get assets around which you could build, before he walks in a year and you get nothing. But the Hornets stood pat and didn\u2019t deal, and it\u2019s a good thing for that franchise. Why should Charlotte be any more inclined to move its best player for pennies on the dollar than, say, the Knicks or the Lakers or any big-market franchise that\u2019s struggling this season? People in North Carolina want value for their entertainment dollars just as much as people in California. It\u2019s hard enough to get free agents to commit to Charlotte; why give away a star guard who, by all accounts, likes it there and wants to stay there? The Raptors made the team around Kyle Lowry and DeMar DeRozan better \u2014 they didn\u2019t blow it up after a couple of playoff failures. The Hornets\u2019 fan base deserves similar restructuring and improvement around Walker rather than a fire sale. 10. Andre Roberson, irreplaceable: The Oklahoma City Thunder guard is out for the season after rupturing his patella tendon Jan. 27 . His impact on the Thunder\u2019s defense has been written about time and time again over the years . The Thunder aren\u2019t the same without him. Yet, in this season where OKC has put all its cards in the middle of the table \u2014 getting Paul George, then trying to keep Paul George by extending Russell Westbrook, then acquiring Carmelo Anthony \u2014 the Thunder didn\u2019t make a deadline move to get a guard to replace Roberson, at least for the rest of the year. * * * OKC was linked to any number of prominent, defense-first wings \u2013 the LA Clippers\u2019 Avery Bradley, Utah\u2019s Hood, the Portland Trail Blazers\u2019 Maurice Harkless \u2014 but didn\u2019t make a deal for any of them. Perhaps the Thunder will make a deal with free agent Tony Allen \u2014 The Grindfather would seem a perfect fit for Roberson\u2019s spot the rest of this year, and the Thunder\u2019s been in contact since the trade deadline passed. But, long-term, assuming a return to health, Roberson will have no significant competition for his minutes or role. On the other hand, some teams did things that were head scratchers, or didn\u2019t seemingly move the needle at all. To paraphrase the dude that former network anchor Dan Rather said attacked him on a Manhattan street in broad daylight in 1986 ( turns out, Rather wasn\u2019t crazy ): * * * 1. The Tale of Tyreke Evans, in Ten Short Chapters: A. He was maybe the most coveted and available player at the trade deadline, in the midst of a great bounceback season after signing a one-year minimum vet deal in Memphis. B. The Grizzlies are going nowhere \u2014 as in a guy sitting at the bus stop who has a game token for Dave and Busters and a coupon for free crazy bread at Little Caesars in his pocket going nowhere \u2014 and Evans was found money, an unexpected asset who could net them something valuable in return. C. The Grizzlies pulled Evans off the court before their game Jan. 31 against the Indiana Pacers , a signal to all of NBA World that they were going to trade him soon and didn\u2019t want him to get injured before a deal could be consummated. D. He continued to sit for more than a week, while the Grizzlies kept losing \u2014 antithetical to the team\u2019s notion that they\u2019re not interested in a rebuld\/tank job this year and think they\u2019ll quickly return to the NBA elite when everyone is healthy. E. The Grizzlies, despite knowing full well that almost no one was\/would be willing to give up a first-round pick in the current almost-everyone-is-capped-out-environment for a player that could turn out to be a three-month rental, insisted on a first-rounder or nothing for Evans . F. No one offered a first-rounder for Evans \u2014 see \u201cE\u201d \u2014 leaving Memphis the option of second-rounders and\/or 2018-19 contracts for him. G. The Grizz, improbably, didn\u2019t move Evans by the deadline, hoping that he truly does, as he\u2019s consistently said, like playing there \u2014 he was a star at the University of Memphis \u2014 and that they can re-sign him in July, despite not having his Bird rights, and add him to their Mike Conley-Marc Gasol nucleus. H. Memphis can, though, get him to Early Bird rights in the summer of 2019 if he were to sign a one-year deal with the Grizz in July, which is the only financial advantage they will have over other teams that could, like Memphis, offer him the full mid-level exception this coming summer. I. But by keeping Evans the rest of this season, Memphis runs the risk of devaluing its own 2018 first-rounder; if he continues to play well, the Grizzlies could win more games and wind up in worse position in the Lottery. J. And if he walks out the door \u2026 well, do they have Dave and Busters locations in the Greater Memphis area? Some of the video games are awesome. 2. Atlanta, holding onto rags in front of Johnny Chan: The Hawks, desperately seeking the bottom of the East to bolster their Lottery chances, didn\u2019t trade any of Kent Bazemore, Dwayne Dedmon, Marco Belinelli or Ersan Ilyasova by the deadline (though they did buy out Belinelli, who\u2019s going to the 76ers ). Maybe the offers for all of them were junk, but, charitably: so what? You don\u2019t give Dedmon away, I guess, but even a second-round pick for Belinelli or Ilyasova would help continue building the Draft stockpile that\u2019s going to be at the heart of any Hawks rebuild the next couple of years. 3. The Brothers Lopez, stuck in neutral: There was buzz around the league that at least one of the two Lopezes would be relocated one way or the other. Brook Lopez, with the Lakers, seemed the liklier candidate; he\u2019s on an expiring deal and has to be renounced by the Lakers in July for them to have the cap space to go after two max free agents, which they can now do after getting Jordan Clarkson\u2019s deal off their books for 2018-19. Robin Lopez is playing very well for the Bulls this season, but he\u2019s got a year left on his deal ($14.3 million), making a trade more likely . But neither Lopez was traded, and as of this writing, neither has been bought out, leaving mascots around the league still vulnerable to the wrath of two seven-footers with chips on their shoulders . 4. The Southeast Division, falling asleep: Okay, Miami brought Wade back, and it was a feel-great story, to be sure. But he\u2019s 36 now, not 26. It wasn\u2019t a balance of power move as much as a balancing of the Heat\u2019s karma. The Wizards and Hawks made a deal for Sheldon Mac , who hasn\u2019t played a minute this season after tearing his Achilles in exhibition play for Washington, and whom Atlanta promptly waived . The Hawks traded Luke Babbitt to Miami for Okaro White, who they promptly waived . Charlotte got Willy Hernangomez from New York for a couple of seconds, and the 23-year-old will no doubt help and be in the Hornets\u2019 rotation. Orlando sent its former first-round pick, Elfrid Payton, to Phoenix for a second-round pick, but didn\u2019t have the fire sale that many around the league thought was coming: no deals for Evan Fournier, Mario Hezonja or Arron Afflalo, much less Aaron Gordon or Nicola Vucevic. It\u2019s not that Atlanta or Orlando had to do something; their big moments will come this summer. But for a trade deadline, it was decidedly underwhelming.  5. Mark Cuban, mostly silent: The Mavericks have almost always made a deal at the deadline, going all the way back to when Don Nelson traded five of his players to the New Jersey Nets in 1997 for four of theirs. (Nellie then told a reporter on the phone of his departing players, \u2019\u2019they\u2019re a bunch of [bleeping] babies. And you can quote me on that.\u201d Since I was the reporter, I did.) But this year, the Mavs didn\u2019t move the expiring contract of Wesley Matthews or Nerlens Noel. Noel hadn\u2019t played well before getting hurt early in the season, and he turned down a four-year, $70 million offer . The Mavs did bring in Doug McDermott as part of a three-team deal that sent Devin Harris to Denver, and maybe McBuckets can finally find a home there. 6. Golden State, lacking nails: (Because the Warriors have a rickety bench. Get it?) The Warriors couldn\u2019t get Johnson or Belinelli, each of whom could have provided production in reserve, following their respective buyouts. Johnson was especially interesting, given that the Warriors saw him as a perfect fit for them, and they\u2019ve almost always gotten their man the last few years. That he chose Houston over the Warriors must cut to the quick. 7. Portland, out of the red: Wheee!! Trading Noah Vonleh to Chicago officially got the Blazers out of luxury tax jail for this year. They\u2019d already done the heavy lifting last July by sending the rest of Allen Crabbe\u2019s $75 million deal to Brooklyn last summer. Moving Vonleh\u2019s $3.5 million to the Bulls just finished the job. And while even owner Paul Allen is entitled to save money when he can, that\u2019s not quite as sexy a move as, say, getting DeAndre Jordan for the stretch drive would have been. 8. Al Jefferson \u2026 you\u2019re still here?: The veteran big man is only playing 13 minutes a night for the Pacers, and that\u2019s understandable. Myles Turner\u2019s in the middle for the bulk of Indiana\u2019s nightly run, and should be. But it\u2019s hard to imagine Jefferson couldn\u2019t have played the Nene role for someone else who still doesn\u2019t mind dumping the ball into the paint every once in a while and watching someone score from there.  9. Georgios Papagiannis, unemployed: Wasn\u2019t the Greek center one of Sacramento\u2019s first-round picks in 2016 ? Wasn\u2019t he part of the reason the Kings traded DeMarcus Cousins, because they had such a promising young big man who wouldn\u2019t cause nearly as much trouble ready to replace him? Didn\u2019t the Kings also acquire Malachi Richardson in the first round in 2016 ? Didn\u2019t they just dump him last week, too ? Okay, they did get the rights to Bogdan Bogdanovic in that 2016 Draft, too. One out of three is \u2026 decent. 10. The Pelicans, quizzical: Already down an All-Star after losing DeMarcus Cousins for the season, and putting Omer Asik into the deal that brought them Nikola Mirotic , give the Nets a solid veteran big in Dante Cunningham \u2026 why?
