He was selected by NBA head coaches as an All-Star reserve and drafted to Team LeBron by captain LeBron James of the Cavaliers. According to NBA rules, when an All-Star is unable to participate, the commissioner shall choose a replacement from the same conference as the player who is being replaced. Love and Dragic both play for Eastern Conference teams. Dragic received the most voting points from NBA head coaches among Eastern Conference players who were not selected as reserves or already named as an injury replacement. The 67th NBA All-Star Game will air on TNT and ESPN Radio and reach fans in more than 200 countries and territories in more than 40 languages through the league\u2019s international television and digital partners. At the time of the deal, the LA Clippers were just one game behind the Nuggets for the final playoff spot in the West. And if the Clippers were going to fade after trading their best player, the Nuggets\u2019 chances of ending a four-year playoff drought were going to increase dramatically. But the Clips are still hanging around , the Nuggets still have some work to do, and the work will be tough in February. Denver has one of the league\u2019s toughest February schedules, with seven of their 10 games against teams that are currently at or above .500. That includes six games against the Warriors, Rockets (x 2), Spurs (x 2) and Thunder. Denver has the league\u2019s toughest February schedule in regard to both opposing offenses and opposing defenses. Through January, the Nuggets are 8-16 against the other 15 teams that are currently at or above .500, having allowed more than 110 points per 100 possessions over those 24 games. Ten of those 16 losses (including two to Boston and San Antonio in the last three days) were games that were within five points in the last five minutes, though. And there is good news with the Nuggets\u2019 February schedule . Only Utah (13.4) and New York (11.9) have bigger home-road NetRtg differentials. The Nuggets also have just one February back-to-back, and the second game is in Phoenix. They have three games this month with a rest advantage (where their opponent played the night before but they did not). The Utah Jazz, coming off wins over Toronto and Golden State, could be Denver\u2019s biggest threat in regard to that last playoff spot. The Nuggets and Jazz have already finished their season series, with each team winning its two home games. But if the Clippers are still hanging around in a few weeks, the Nuggets\u2019 most important February game could be their last, when they host LA on Feb. 27. Note: Every team has at least seven full days off for the All-Star break. Two teams \u2013 Dallas and San Antonio \u2013 have the longest All-Star breaks: nine days off between games. Rest advantage \/ Rest disadvantage: Games in which one team (at a disadvantage) played the day before and the other (at an advantage) did not. Teams are currently 120-82 (.594) with a rest advantage, 98-49 (.667) at home and 22-33 (.400) on the road. Things could certainly come together for the Wizards if Wall returns healthier and stronger in April and May (they won\u2019t have to play the Nets or Mavs in the playoffs), but as they look to stay in the mix for a top four seed in the East, they\u2019ll have a difficult schedule to navigate without one of their All-Stars. That Golden State game will be only the second game of 12 straight against teams that are currently over .500. The Wizards\u2019 March might be tougher than their February, and just staying in playoff position at all could be a challenge. Johnson, a seven-time All-Star, signed a reported two-year deal in the summer of 2016 and will be an unrestricted free agent this summer."},{"id":47772,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/joe-prunty-tackles-task-guiding-milwaukee-bucks-path-rest-season","date":"2018-02-01","title":"Interim coach Joe Prunty tackles task of guiding Milwaukee Bucks' path","content":"It\u2019s an oldie but an NBA goodie, the description that the late Hall of Famer Chuck Daly came up with to describe what he and the league\u2019s other coaches do for a living. \u201cCoaching is like flying an airplane,\u201d said Daly, a two-time NBA champion with the Detroit Pistons and coach of the original \u201cDream Team\u201d in the 1992 Olympics. \u201cThere is going to be a lot of turbulence, but your job is to land the plane safely.\u201d For the someone thrust into that role in mid-flight the way Milwaukee Bucks interim coach Joe Prunty was last week when the Bucks fired Jason Kidd , this isn\u2019t simply a co-pilot sliding over one seat to replace the captain. Once that \u201cinterim\u201d light flashes on, with the plane still 35,000 feet up but adrift, a team might as well be plucking its pilot \u201cAirplane!\u201d-style from the main cabin . The change is that abrupt. The challenges, that great. \u201cGenerally speaking, your job is to get through the year,\u201d said P.J. Carlesimo, longtime coach and broadcaster who has been both \u201cinterim\u201d and \u201cinterimed\u201d in his career. \u201cAnd usually it\u2019s not a good team. Your good teams don\u2019t usually make these changes. \u201cThe trick is having good players. Knowing Joe and the way he is, I\u2019m sure he\u2019ll tell you the same thing.\u201d The Bucks were 23-22 on Jan. 22 when management fired Kidd, the soon-to-be Hall of Fame point guard who had coached the team since 2014. Kidd met the early expectations of new franchise ownership by steering the Bucks to the playoffs in two of his first three seasons. But his overall record was 139-152, and 2017-18 was playing out fitfully, with no momentum, no traction. When Kidd tried to tamp down expectations after a dreary post-Christmas performance against Chicago, this season no longer just seemed like \u2014 it sounded like \u2014 a lost opportunity. \u201cIt just felt like we were standing still when we should be climbing,\u201d Milwaukee\u2019s first-year general manager, Jon Horst, told the Milwaukee Journal Sentinel . \u201cThis is an important year.\u201d No kidding. Milwaukee is a franchise aiming at big things . A massive new arena to replace the BMO Harris Bradley Center needs to be filled come fall. The team\u2019s tri-owners \u2014 Marc Lasry, Wes Edens and Jamie Dinan, all private-equity movers and shakers \u2014 rejected from the start former Bucks steward Herb Kohl\u2019s smaller-market mission of simply keeping the team competitive from year to year. The new guys want championships. This season was targeted as a step toward that, with Milwaukee seeking a top-four playoff seed and advancement to the conference semifinals. Those were important goals for external and internal reasons. Giannis Antetokounmpo, 23, the team\u2019s most talented player, is on the cusp of NBA superstardom and is under contract only through the 2020-21 season. Jabari Parker, if he comes back successfully from his second knee surgery in three seasons (he\u2019s set to play 15 minutes against New York Friday ), will be a restricted free agent this summer. And keeping a young, talented core together is tough enough, never mind adding pieces in a city not considered much of a free-agent destination. * Blogtable:  Can Bucks make push for No. 3 in East? Prunty\u2019s new job is far more focused than that and, so far, so good: the Bucks were 4-0 through his first eight days as Kidd\u2019s replacement, with back-to-back games at Minnesota tonight ( 8 ET, NBA League Pass ) and Friday vs. New York ( 8 ET, NBA League Pass ). At that pace, they\u2019d run the table, finish with a tidy 60-22 mark, be sitting right where they want to be in the standings and have the rest of the East scared to death. Now in his 22nd NBA season, Prunty, 48, isn\u2019t going anywhere near that sort of nonsense. He\u2019s fine as a plugger, thank you, with a strict see-the-game, play-the-game approach. If he comes up with any Dalyesque analogies, it will be by accident \u2014 or he\u2019ll be quoting someone he\u2019s worked with, like San Antonio Spurs coach Gregg Popovich, former Mavs and Nets coach Avery Johnson, former Cleveland Cavaliers coach Byron Scott or Indiana Pacers coach Nate McMillan (Prunty was on his staff in Portland) or Kidd. \u201cThe teams that win in this league are the teams that win in this league,\u201d said Prunty, a native Californian who coached Lakers coach Luke Walton and former Chicago Cubs pitcher Mark Prior in high school. \u201cYou will have success based on what everybody does to contribute to that. \u2026 It is about getting better day over day. It always sounds boring and like a clich\u00e9, but it is the truth.\u201d \u201cInterim\u201d is a tricky position. Too much old or too much new could be bad. Whatever the previous guy was doing, that got him fired, so don\u2019t do that. But if you try to change too many things on the fly, that could create problems where they don\u2019t exist. Players who have come to know you as an advocate for the fired guy\u2019s system will wonder you really embrace. The \u201cgood cop\u201d role many assistants play will require some \u201cbad cop\u201d decisions now. Meanwhile, there\u2019s job security in play. Prunty has the position for the rest of Milwaukee\u2019s season, but immediately upon Kidd\u2019s firing, national pundits were calling the job \u201cone of the most sought-after\u201d in the NBA. \u201cYou don\u2019t want to mess it up,\u201d Carlesimo said. \u201cIt\u2019s a tremendous advantage being on the inside. You know all the players, they know you. You can change the rotations, you can change whatever you want. But the vast majority of the plays, the playbook, stays the same.\u201d Through the first week of the Prunty era, Milwaukee has demonstrated more tweaks than overhaul. Hidden within the team\u2019s overall offensive ( 107.7, 8th overall ) and defensive ( 106.7, 20th overall ) ratings are these monsters: the Bucks\u2019 offensive rating is 116.6 and their defensive rating is 95.1 during this 4-0 run \u2014 numbers that would rank No. 1 in both categories. It helps immensely to have faced the Phoenix Suns, Brooklyn Nets, Chicago Bulls (without Kris Dunn) and Philadelphia 76ers (without All-Star Joel Embiid) in those games. But the Bucks have noticed X & O adjustments, while talking about a change in atmosphere as well. \u201cRight now, you can tell guys are a little bit looser,\u201d guard Khris Middleton said. \u201cWith Joe, he preaches confidence. His plays are designed for us to move the ball side to side more. And just, not necessarily just playing off one matchup, but just trying to use the matchup as a decoy to get other guys shots.\u201d Antetokounmpo claimed to see no tactical differences, citing Prunty\u2019s influence even before Kidd\u2019s dismissal. But he did say that \u201cguys are playing harder.\u201d \u201cTeams usually take on the personality of the coach,\u201d Middleton added. \u201cWith Joe, he\u2019s a lot more relaxed, much more of a pick-a-guy-up type of guy and you kind of see that with the guys out here.\u201d Said Carlesimo: \u201cObviously the players there have responded. It usually goes one way or the other \u2014 players play well or they pack it in. The lame excuses aren\u2019t there anymore, so it\u2019s \u2018Hey, step up! If you or your agent or the media was implying there was something wrong with the coaching, here\u2019s your chance to show it.\u2019 \u201d Carlesimo went through this five years ago in Brooklyn, when Johnson was fired after a 14-14 start in 2012-13 . He moved over the proverbial 18 inches on the Nets bench and led them to a 35-19 mark the rest of the way. Things soured for that team \u2014 built around Joe Johnson, Deron Williams and Brook Lopez \u2014 only when it lost in the first round (dropping Game 7 at Barclay Center) to a Chicago club using journeyman Nate Robinson in injured Derrick Rose\u2019s role. That summer, Brooklyn cleaned house and hired Kidd, who hired Prunty. And so it goes. \u201c \u2018Interim\u2019 clearly is an audition,\u201d Carlesimo said. \u201cThere have been guys who were interim and got the job full-time. But that\u2019s usually not the way it goes. Management ends up going outside to change direction. \u201cIt\u2019s really going to come down to what the Bucks owners and Jon Horst think. It\u2019s Joe\u2019s job to land the plane.\u201d * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. You can e-mail him  here , find  his archive here  and  follow him on Twitter .
